id="Quickstart">Installation</h2>
<p>Installing React Hook Form only takes a single command and you&#x27;re ready to roll.</p>
<div style="position:relative"><div class="CodeArea_buttonWrapper__mOP59"><button class="CodeArea_button__OHC50 CodeArea_copyButton__GWEJK" aria-label="Copy code into your clipboard.">Copy</button></div><div><pre class="prism-code language-bash" style="background-color:var(--color-purple);color:#f8f8f2"><div class="token-line" style="color:#f8f8f2"><span class="token plain">npm install react-hook-form</span></div></pre></div></div>

<h2 id="ReactWebVideoTutorial">React Web Video Tutorial</h2>
<p>This video tutorial illustrates the basic usage and concepts of React Hook Form.</p>
<div data-testid="general-observer"><iframe data-testid="youtube" title="youTube-RkXv4AXXC_4" src="https://www.youtube.com/embed/RkXv4AXXC_4?&amp;autoplay=false" frameBorder="0" allow="accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture" allowfullscreen="" width="100%" height="500"></iframe></div>
<h2 id="Registerfields">Register fields</h2>
<p>One of the key concepts in React Hook Form is to <strong><code>register</code></strong> your component into the hook. This will make its value available for both the form validation and submission.</p>
<p><strong>Note:</strong> Each field is <strong>required</strong> to have a <code>name</code> as a key for the registration process.</p>

<h2 id="Applyvalidation">Apply validation</h2>
<p>React Hook Form makes form validation easy by aligning with the existing <a href="https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Learn/HTML/Forms/Form_validation">HTML standard for form validation</a>.</p>
<p>List of validation rules supported:</p>
<ul>
<li>required</li>
<li>min</li>
<li>max</li>
<li>minLength</li>
<li>maxLength</li>
<li>pattern</li>
<li>validate</li>
</ul>
<p>You can read more detail on each rule in the <a href="/docs#register">register section</a>.</p>

<h2 id="Integratinganexistingform">Integrating an existing form</h2>
<p>Integrating an existing form should be simple. The important step is to <code>register</code> the component&#x27;s <code>ref</code> and assign relevant props to your input.</p>

<h2 id="IntegratingwithUIlibraries">Integrating with UI libraries</h2>
<p>React Hook Form has made it easy to integrate with external UI component libraries. If the component doesn&#x27;t expose input&#x27;s <code>ref</code>, then you should use the <a href="/docs#Controller">Controller</a> component, which will take care of the registration process.</p>

<h2 id="IntegratingControlledInputs">Integrating Controlled Inputs</h2>
<p>This library embraces uncontrolled components and native HTML inputs. However, it&#x27;s hard to avoid working with external controlled components such as <a href="https://ui.shadcn.com/docs/components/form">shadcn/ui</a>, <a href="https://github.com/JedWatson/react-select">React-Select</a>, <a href="https://github.com/ant-design/ant-design">AntD</a> and <a href="https://mui.com/">MUI</a>. To make this simple, we provide a wrapper component, <a href="/docs#Controller">Controller</a>, to streamline the integration process while still giving you the freedom to use a custom register.</p>
<h4>Using Component API</h4>

<h2 id="Integratingwithglobalstate">Integrating with global state</h2>
<p>This library doesn&#x27;t require you to rely on a state management library, but you can easily integrate with them.</p>

<h2 id="Handleerrors">Handle errors</h2>
<p>React Hook Form provides an <code>errors</code> object to show you the errors in the form. <code>errors</code>&#x27; type will return given validation constraints. The following example showcases a required validation rule.</p>

<h2 id="Integratingwithservices">Integrating with services</h2>
<p>To integrate React Hook Form with a service, you can use the library&#x27;s built-in submission handling. <code>&lt;Form /&gt;</code> component allow you to easily send form data to an API endpoint or other service. <a href="/docs/useform/form">Find out more about Form component</a>.</p>

<h2 id="SchemaValidation">Schema Validation</h2>
<p>We also support schema-based form validation with <a href="https://github.com/jquense/yup">Yup</a>, <a href="https://github.com/vriad/zod">Zod</a> , <a href="https://github.com/ianstormtaylor/superstruct">Superstruct</a> &amp; <a href="https://github.com/hapijs/joi">Joi</a>, where you can pass your <code>schema</code> to <a href="/docs#useForm">useForm</a> as an optional config. It will validate your input data against the schema and return with either <a href="/docs#errors">errors</a> or a valid result.</p>
<p><strong>Step 1:</strong> Install <code>Yup</code> into your project.</p>
<div style="position:relative"><div class="CodeArea_buttonWrapper__mOP59"><button class="CodeArea_button__OHC50 CodeArea_copyButton__GWEJK" aria-label="Copy code into your clipboard.">Copy</button></div><div><pre class="prism-code language-bash" style="background-color:var(--color-purple);color:#f8f8f2"><div class="token-line" style="color:#f8f8f2"><span class="token plain">npm install @hookform/resolvers yup</span></div></pre></div></div>
<p><strong>Step 2:</strong> Prepare your schema for validation and register inputs with React Hook Form.</p>

<h2 id="ReactNative">React Native</h2>
<p>You will get the same performance boost and enhancement in React Native. To integrate with input component, you can wrap it with <code>Controller</code>.</p>

<h2 id="TypeScript">TypeScript</h2>
<p>React Hook Form is built with <code>TypeScript</code>, and you can define a <code>FormData</code> type to support form values.</p>

<h2 id="Designandphilosophy">Design and philosophy</h2>
<p>React Hook Form&#x27;s design and philosophy focus on user and developer experience. The library aims to provide users with a smoother interaction experience by fine-tuning the performance and improving accessibility. Some of the performance enhancements include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Introducing form state subscription model through the proxy</li>
<li>Avoiding unnecessary computation</li>
<li>Isolating component re-rendering when required</li>
</ul>
<p>Overall, it improves the user experience while users interact with the application. As for the developers, we introduce built-in validation and are closely aligned with HTML standards allowing further extension with powerful validation methods and integration with schema validation natively. In addition, having a strongly type-checked form with the help of typescript provides early build-time feedback to help and guide the developer to build a robust form solution.</p>
<p>The following talk given by <a href="https://twitter.com/bluebill1049">Bill</a> showcased some of the ideas and design patterns:</p>

{#ReactWebVideoTutorial}\n\nThis video tutorial illustrates the basic usage and concepts of React Hook Form.\n\n\u003cYouTube youTubeId=\"RkXv4AXXC_4\" /\u003e\n\n## Register fields {#Registerfields}\n\nOne of the key concepts in React Hook Form is to **`register`** your component into the hook. This will make its value available for both the form validation and submission.\n\n**Note:** Each field is **required** to have a `name` as a key for the registration process.\n\n{/* JSTSCopy [CodeSandbox JS](https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-get-started-smspp) */}\n\n\u003cTabGroup buttonLabels={[\"TS\", \"JS\"]} \u003e\n\n```tsx copy {#Applyvalidation}\n\nReact Hook Form makes form validation easy by aligning with the existing [HTML standard for form validation](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Learn/HTML/Forms/Form_validation).\n\nList of validation rules supported:\n\n- required\n- min\n- max\n- minLength\n- maxLength\n- pattern\n- validate\n\nYou can read more detail on each rule in the [register section](/docs#register).\n\n\u003cTabGroup buttonLabels={[\"TS\", \"JS\"]} \u003e\n\n```tsx copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-apply-validation-ts-forked-nmbyh\"\nimport { useForm, SubmitHandler } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\ninterface IFormInput {\n  firstName: string\n  lastName: string\n  age: number\n}\n\nexport default function App() {\n  const { register, handleSubmit } = useForm\u003cIFormInput\u003e()\n  const onSubmit: SubmitHandler\u003cIFormInput\u003e = (data) =\u003e console.log(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"firstName\", { required: true, maxLength: 20 })} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"lastName\", { pattern: /^[A-Za-z]+$/i })} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"number\" {...register(\"age\", { min: 18, max: 99 })} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-apply-validation-q5m00\"\nimport { useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\nexport type=\"number\" {...register(\"age\", { min: 18, max: 99 })} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n\u003c/TabGroup\u003e\n\n## Integrating an existing form {#Integratinganexistingform}\n\nIntegrating an existing form should be simple. The important step is to `register` the component's `ref` and assign relevant props to your input.\n\n\u003cTabGroup buttonLabels={[\"TS\", \"JS\"]} \u003e\n\n```tsx copy with external UI component libraries. If the component doesn't expose input's `ref`, then you should use the [Controller](/docs#Controller) component, which will take care of the registration process.\n\n\u003cTabGroup buttonLabels={[\"TS\", \"JS\"]} \u003e\n\n```tsx copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-with-ui-library-ts-forked-qjgkx\"\nimport Select from \"react-select\"\nimport { useForm, value: string }\n}\n\nconst App = () =\u003e {\n  const { control, handleSubmit } = useForm({\n    defaultValues: {\n      firstName: \"\",\n      lastName: \"\",\n      iceCreamType: {},\n    },\n \u003cController\n        name=\"firstName\"\n        control={control}\n        render={({ field }) =\u003e \u003cInput {...field} /\u003e}\n      /\u003e\n      \u003cController\n  /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-with-ui-library-forked-fp5r3\"\nimport          { value: \"chocolate\", label: \"Chocolate\" },\n              { value: \"strawberry\", label: \"Strawberry\" },\n              { value: \"vanilla\", label: \"Vanilla\" },\n            ]}\n {#IntegratingControlledInputs}\n\nThis library embraces uncontrolled components and native HTML inputs. However, it's hard to avoid working with external controlled components such as [shadcn/ui](https://ui.shadcn.com/docs/components/form), [React-Select](https://github.com/JedWatson/react-select), [AntD](https://github.com/ant-design/ant-design) and [MUI](https://mui.com/). To make this simple, we provide a wrapper component, [Controller](/docs#Controller), to streamline the integration process while still giving you the freedom to use a custom register.\n\n#### Using Component API\n\n\u003cTabGroup buttonLabels={[\"TS\", \"JS\", 'shadcn/ui']} \u003e\n\n```tsx copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-v6-controller-ts-jwyzw\"\nimport { useForm, Controller, SubmitHandler } from \"react-hook-form\"\nimport { TextField, Checkbox } from \"@material-ui/core\"\n\ninterface IFormInputs {\n  TextField: string\n  MyCheckbox: boolean\n}\n\nfunction App() {\n  const { handleSubmit, control, reset } = useForm\u003cIFormInputs\u003e({\n    defaultValues: {\n      MyCheckbox: false,\n    },\n  })\n  const onSubmit: SubmitHandler\u003cIFormInputs\u003e = (data) =\u003e console.log(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n      \u003cController\n        name=\"MyCheckbox\"\n        control={control}\n        rules={{ required: true }}\n        render={({ field }) =\u003e \u003cCheckbox {...field} /\u003e}\n      /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-v7-controller-5h1q5\"\nimport { TextField } from \"@material-ui/core\"\nimport { useController, useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\nfunction Input({ control, name }) {\n  const {\n    field,\n    fieldState: { invalid, isTouched, isDirty },\n    formState: { touchedFields, dirtyFields },\n  } = useController({\n    name,\n    control,\n    rules: { required: true },\n  })\n\n  return (\n    \u003cTextField\n      onChange={field.onChange} // send value to hook form\n      onBlur={field.onBlur} // notify when input is touched/blur\n      value={field.value} // input value\n      name={field.name} // send down the input name\n      inputRef={field.ref} // send input ref, so we can focus on input when error appear\n    /\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n```javascript copy\nimport { zodResolver } from \"@hookform/resolvers/zod\"\nimport { useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\nimport { z } from \"zod\"\nimport { Form, FormControl, FormField } from \"@/components/ui/form\"\nimport { Input } from \"@/components/ui/input\"\n\nconst FormSchema = z.object({\n  username: z.string().min(2, {\n    message: \"Username must be at least 2 characters.\",\n  }),\n})\n\nexport function InputForm() {\n  const form = useForm({\n    resolver: zodResolver(FormSchema),\n    defaultValues: {\n      username: \"\",\n    },\n  })\n\n  function onSubmit(data: z.output\u003ctypeof FormSchema\u003e) {\n    console.log(data);\n  }\n\n  return (\n    \u003cForm {...form}\u003e\n      \u003cform onSubmit={form.handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n        \u003cFormField\n          control={form.control}\n          name=\"username\"\n          render={({ field }) =\u003e (\n            \u003cFormControl\u003e\u003cInput {...field} /\u003e\u003c/FormControl\u003e\n          )}\n        /\u003e\n        \u003cbutton type=\"submit\"\u003eSubmit\u003c/button\u003e\n      \u003c/form\u003e\n    \u003c/Form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n\u003c/TabGroup\u003e\n\n#### Using Hooks API\n\n\u003cTabGroup buttonLabels={[\"TS\", \"JS\"]} \u003e\n\n```tsx copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/usecontroller-forked-4t8cx\"\nimport * as React from \"react\"\nimport { useForm, useController, UseControllerProps } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\ntype FormValues = {\n  FirstName: string\n}\n\nfunction Input(props: UseControllerProps\u003cFormValues\u003e) {\n  const { field, fieldState } = useController(props)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cdiv\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...field} placeholder={props.name} /\u003e\n      \u003cp\u003e{fieldState.isTouched \u0026\u0026 \"Touched\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n      \u003cp\u003e{fieldState.isDirty \u0026\u0026 \"Dirty\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n      \u003cp\u003e{fieldState.invalid ? \"invalid\" : \"valid\"}\u003c/p\u003e\n    \u003c/div\u003e\n  )\n}\n\nexport default function App() {\n  const { handleSubmit, control } = useForm\u003cFormValues\u003e({\n    defaultValues: {\n      FirstName: \"\",\n    },\n    mode: \"onChange\",\n  })\n  const onSubmit = (data: FormValues) =\u003e console.log(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n      \u003cInput control={control} name=\"FirstName\" rules={{ required: true }} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/usecontroller-tefsc\"\nimport { TextField } from \"@material-ui/core\"\nimport { useController, useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\nfunction Input({ control, name }) {\n  const {\n    field,\n    fieldState: { invalid, isTouched, isDirty },\n    formState: { touchedFields, dirtyFields },\n  } = useController({\n    name,\n    control,\n    rules: { required: true },\n  })\n\n  return (\n    \u003cTextField\n      onChange={field.onChange} // send value to hook form\n      onBlur={field.onBlur} // notify when input is touched/blur\n      value={field.value} // input value\n      name={field.name} // send down the input name\n      inputRef={field.ref} // send input ref, so we can focus on input when error appear\n    /\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n\u003c/TabGroup\u003e\n\n## Integrating with global state {#Integratingwithglobalstate}\n\nThis library doesn't require you to rely on a state management library, but you can easily integrate with them.\n\n```javascript copy\nimport { useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\nimport { connect } from \"react-redux\"\nimport updateAction from \"./actions\"\n\nexport default function App(props) {\n  const { register, handleSubmit, setValue } = useForm({\n    defaultValues: {\n      firstName: \"\",\n      lastName: \"\",\n    },\n  })\n  // Submit your data into Redux store\n  const onSubmit = (data) =\u003e props.updateAction(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"firstName\")} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"lastName\")} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n\n// Connect your component with redux\nconnect(\n  ({ firstName, lastName }) =\u003e ({ firstName, lastName }),\n  updateAction\n)(YourForm)\n```\n\n## Handle errors {#Handleerrors}\n\nReact Hook Form provides an `errors` object to show you the errors in the form. `errors`' type will return given validation constraints. The following example showcases a required validation rule.\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-v7-errormessage-multiple-error-messages-3ur2z\"\nimport { useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\nexport default function App() {\n  const {\n    register,\n    formState: { errors },\n    handleSubmit,\n  } = useForm()\n  const onSubmit = (data) =\u003e console.log(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n      \u003cinput\n        {...register(\"firstName\", { required: true })}\n        aria-invalid={errors.firstName ? \"true\" : \"false\"}\n      /\u003e\n      {errors.firstName?.type === \"required\" \u0026\u0026 (\n        \u003cp role=\"alert\"\u003eFirst name is required\u003c/p\u003e\n      )}\n\n      \u003cinput\n        {...register(\"mail\", { required: \"Email Address is required\" })}\n        aria-invalid={errors.mail ? \"true\" : \"false\"}\n      /\u003e\n      {errors.mail \u0026\u0026 \u003cp role=\"alert\"\u003e{errors.mail.message}\u003c/p\u003e}\n\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n## Integrating with services {#Integratingwithservices}\n\nTo integrate React Hook Form with a service, you can use the library's built-in submission handling. `\u003cForm /\u003e` component allow you to easily send form data to an API endpoint or other service. [Find out more about Form component](/docs/useform/form).\n\n```javascript\nimport { Form } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\nfunction App() {\n  const { register, control } = useForm()\n\n  return (\n    \u003cForm\n      action=\"/api/save\" // Send post request with the FormData\n      // encType={'application/json'} you can also switch to json object\n      onSuccess={() =\u003e {\n        alert(\"Your application is updated.\")\n      }}\n      onError={() =\u003e {\n        alert(\"Submission has failed.\")\n      }}\n      control={control}\n    \u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"firstName\", { required: true })} /\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"lastName\", { required: true })} /\u003e\n      \u003cbutton\u003eSubmit\u003c/button\u003e\n    \u003c/Form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n## Schema Validation {#SchemaValidation}\n\nWe also support schema-based form validation with [Yup](https://github.com/jquense/yup), [Zod](https://github.com/vriad/zod) , [Superstruct](https://github.com/ianstormtaylor/superstruct) \u0026 [Joi](https://github.com/hapijs/joi), where you can pass your `schema` to [useForm](/docs#useForm) as an optional config. It will validate your input data against the schema and return with either [errors](/docs#errors) or a valid result.\n\n**Step 1:** Install `Yup` into your project.\n\n```bash copy\nnpm install @hookform/resolvers yup\n```\n\n**Step 2:** Prepare your schema for validation and register inputs with React Hook Form.\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-v7-validationschema-rm35t\"\nimport { useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\nimport { yupResolver } from \"@hookform/resolvers/yup\"\nimport * as yup from \"yup\"\n\nconst schema = yup\n  .object({\n    firstName: yup.string().required(),\n    age: yup.number().positive().integer().required(),\n  })\n  .required()\n\nexport default function App() {\n  const {\n    register,\n    handleSubmit,\n    formState: { errors },\n  } = useForm({\n    resolver: yupResolver(schema),\n  })\n  const onSubmit = (data) =\u003e console.log(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={handleSubmit(onSubmit)}\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"firstName\")} /\u003e\n      \u003cp\u003e{errors.firstName?.message}\u003c/p\u003e\n\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"age\")} /\u003e\n      \u003cp\u003e{errors.age?.message}\u003c/p\u003e\n\n      \u003cinput type=\"submit\" /\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n## React Native {#ReactNative}\n\nYou will get the same performance boost and enhancement in React Native. To integrate with input component, you can wrap it with `Controller`.\n\n```javascript copy sandbox=\"https://snack.expo.io/@bluebill1049/react-hook-form-v7---controller\" expo\nimport { Text, View, TextInput, Button, Alert } from \"react-native\"\nimport { useForm, Controller } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\nexport default function App() {\n  const {\n    control,\n    handleSubmit,\n    formState: { errors },\n  } = useForm({\n    defaultValues: {\n      firstName: \"\",\n      lastName: \"\",\n    },\n  })\n  const onSubmit = (data) =\u003e console.log(data)\n\n  return (\n    \u003cView\u003e\n      \u003cController\n        control={control}\n        rules={{\n          required: true,\n        }}\n        render={({ field: { onChange, onBlur, value } }) =\u003e (\n          \u003cTextInput\n            placeholder=\"First name\"\n            onBlur={onBlur}\n            onChangeText={onChange}\n            value={value}\n          /\u003e\n        )}\n        name=\"firstName\"\n      /\u003e\n      {errors.firstName \u0026\u0026 \u003cText\u003eThis is required.\u003c/Text\u003e}\n\n      \u003cController\n        control={control}\n        rules={{\n          maxLength: 100,\n        }}\n        render={({ field: { onChange, onBlur, value } }) =\u003e (\n          \u003cTextInput\n            placeholder=\"Last name\"\n            onBlur={onBlur}\n            onChangeText={onChange}\n            value={value}\n          /\u003e\n        )}\n        name=\"lastName\"\n      /\u003e\n\n      \u003cButton title=\"Submit\" onPress={handleSubmit(onSubmit)} /\u003e\n    \u003c/View\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n## TypeScript {#TypeScript}\n\nReact Hook Form is built with `TypeScript`, and you can define a `FormData` type to support form values.\n\n```tsx copy sandbox=\"https://codesandbox.io/s/react-hook-form-typescript-qwk7b\"\nimport * as React from \"react\"\nimport { useForm } from \"react-hook-form\"\n\ntype FormData = {\n  firstName: string\n  lastName: string\n}\n\nexport default function App() {\n  const {\n    register,\n    setValue,\n    handleSubmit,\n    formState: { errors },\n  } = useForm\u003cFormData\u003e()\n  const onSubmit = handleSubmit((data) =\u003e console.log(data))\n  // firstName and lastName will have correct type\n\n  return (\n    \u003cform onSubmit={onSubmit}\u003e\n      \u003clabel\u003eFirst Name\u003c/label\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"firstName\")} /\u003e\n      \u003clabel\u003eLast Name\u003c/label\u003e\n      \u003cinput {...register(\"lastName\")} /\u003e\n      \u003cbutton\n        type=\"button\"\n        onClick={() =\u003e {\n          setValue(\"lastName\", \"luo\") // ✅\n          setValue(\"firstName\", true) // ❌: true is not string\n          errors.bill // ❌: property bill does not exist\n        }}\n      \u003e\n        SetValue\n      \u003c/button\u003e\n    \u003c/form\u003e\n  )\n}\n```\n\n## Design and philosophy {#Designandphilosophy}\n\nReact Hook Form's design and philosophy focus on user and developer experience. The library aims to provide users with a smoother interaction experience by fine-tuning the performance and improving accessibility. Some of the performance enhancements include:\n\n- Introducing form state subscription model through the proxy\n- Avoiding unnecessary computation\n- Isolating component re-rendering when required\n\nOverall, it improves the user experience while users interact with the application. As for the developers, we introduce built-in validation and are closely aligned with HTML standards allowing further extension with powerful validation methods and integration with schema validation natively. In addition, having a strongly type-checked form with the help of typescript provides early build-time feedback to help and guide the developer to build a robust form solution.\n\nThe following talk given by [Bill](https://twitter.com/bluebill1049) showcased some of the ideas and design patterns:\n\n\u003cYouTube youTubeId=\"ZFxHdpzaEmM\" /\u003e\n","code":"var Component=(()=\u003e{var
